4.2
Project Development
The development of the project was basically divided in 3 steps.
1. Development of dierent congurations of an integrated gasication, SOFCs,
steam cycle and absorption chiller plant for the trigeneration of electricity,
heating and cooling. Six dierent congurations are investigated.
2. Optimization of the six congurations under study to see the potentiality
of each solution.
3. Economic analysis of plants investigated developed.
4.2.1
Development of dierent Designs o the Plant
The problem of municipal solid waste management has not to be underesti-
mated. The combustion of waste has long been a good alternative to the landll.
==PAGE:84==
60
Software and Methods
Actually the gasication of waste represents a good alternative to combustion.
The syngas produced by the gasication process has high energy content and
can be used to produce electricity in dierent ways. In this investigation is cho-
sen to send the synthesis gas derived from gasication to a SOFC plant.
The energy content of the o-fuel and o-air from a SOFC plant can be used by
letting the combustion occur into a catalytic burner [43]. The ue gas produced
is then introduced into the heat recovery steam generator of a steam cycle.
Flue gas temperature after the HRSG is still high enough to be used with an
absorption chiller. The model of the chiller is studied to reach a coecient of
performance around 0.61, any pressure drop is theoretically considered in the
model of this plant.
Dierent ue gas temperatures after the heat recovery
steam generator cause dierent ow rates of the lithium bromide solution cir-
culating in the chiller. The lithium bromide mass ow is responsible for higher
or lower cooling power production. With the conguration briey introduced it
is possible to produce electricity, heating and cooling.
The rst conguration of the plant supposes an anode pre-heater before the
SOFCs, this component recovers some heat of the o-fuel to pre-heat the syngas
entering the anode. Rokni shows in [36] as by substituting the anode pre-heater
with a methanator the eciency of the plant improves. One more congura-
tion of the plant is developed employing the methanator instead of the anode
pre-heater. The solution with the methanator reaches higher performances as
expected.
A further improvement of the conguration was obtained by introducing the
hybrid recuperator as explained in [28]. The introduction of hybrid recuperator
before the cathode pre-heater improves the thermal eciency of the plant in
both congurations, with anode pre-heater and with mathanator. The design
change shows that the eciency improvement is higher in the solution with an-
ode pre-heater.
After the introduction of the hybrid recuperator, the behaviour of the system
is investigated by splitting the total amount of SOFC stacks. This analysis is
conducted for both congurations under study, with anode pre-heater and with
methanator. The solutions found out for the plants have some dierences in
blocks disposal. The anode pre-heater design allows to recover some heat into
the anode pre-heater after the rst block of stacks. The energy of the o-air com-
ing out from the second block of stack can be used in the cathode pre-heater
before going into the burner as oxidant.
Concerning the plant design with
methanator, the energy recovery at the cathode pre-heater is possible. Because
of this, the improvement of thermal eciency in the solution with mathanator
is lower than in the other case. The blocks disposal does not allow the same
operating temperature and the same utilization factor for both of them, detailed
working conditions of the plants are shown in Chapter 6. It has to be noticed
that the use of dierent components (anode pre-heater and methanator) and
the plant complexity lead to dierent operating congurations. The analysis
of the results allows to establish the most performing solution under the same
==PAGE:85==
4.2 Project Development
61
working conditions.
4.2.2
Optimization of the Plants Designed
Six dierent congurations are studied with small changes in input data to allow
the correct operation, this data are examined in detail in Chapter 5. After the
development of the six working plants the focus was on solid oxide fuel cells.
The sensitivity analysis was carried out by changing SOFC parameters. On the
basis of this sensitivity analysis each plant was optimized in terms of thermal
eciency (LHV) expressed by Equation 4.28 [37].
ηth,plant =

Pnet
˙mfuelLHVfuel

(4.28)
The study allows to see the potentiality of dierent congurations. The opti-
mization was carried out by analysing the following parameters:
 SOFCs operating temperature,
 SOFCs utilization factor,
 SOFCs number of stacks.
An optimized solution is obtained for each plant. The high thermal eciency
(LHV) values are reached for congurations with two stack blocks. Through the
analysis done it is possible to observe which of the solutions reaches the best
eciency with particular working parameters.
4.2.3
Economic Analysis
The nal step of the project consists in the economic analysis. All the plants
designed, before and after the optimization process are subjected to this analysis,
the results of the study are shown in Chapter 7.
Dierent spreadsheets for each component of the plant are realized by using
the software Microsoft Excel©. The purchased equipment cost (PEC) is rstly
evaluated for each component and then for the total pant. The total PEC is
obtained by summing up the PEC of each component.
==PAGE:86==
62
Software and Methods
Additional costs are divided into direct and indirect costs and calculated. Direct
costs can be classied in on-site costs and o-site costs as schematized in Figure
4.4.
Figure 4.4: Block diagram of additional cost. Inspired to [59].
The additional costs are expressed as a percentage of the PEC, Table 4.2 shows
the values of this percentage.
On-site costs are 93% of PEC while the o-site costs are 56% of PEC, meaning
that the total contribution of direct costs is 149% of the PEC. The increase
of the price due to indirect costs is 26.45% of PEC. The total contribution of
additional costs to the total investment cost (TIC) is about 175% of PEC.
The spreadsheet provides also the calculation of the total investment cost, this
is the result of the sum of PEC and additional costs.
Total
Investment
Cost
(TIC) =
Purchased
Equipment
Cost

4.2.3.1
Payback Time
The estimation of the components cost is done by using the formulas shown in
Appendix A. A relation for the price evaluation is found for each component
except the mixer. This element does not have a considerable importance on
the total balance and, for this reason, it is considered negligible. The model
adopted for the calculation of the payback time is briey explained here. The
net present value for each year is evaluated with the well known formula shown
in Equation 4.29
NPV =
N
X
n=0
Cn
(1 + r)n = C0 +
N
X
n=1
Cn
(1 + r)n
(4.29)
where n is the time period in years, Cn is the net cash ow during the year n
==PAGE:88==
64
Software and Methods
and r is the discount rate. C0 is the initial expanse for the plant, it is equal to
the total investment cost and it must be considered negative. The payback is
reached when the NPV becomes equal to zero. In this investigation the total
number of operating years of the plant is set at 20 [60] and the discount rate
value was xed at 0.04 [61]. The net cash ow of a time period is evaluated as
the dierence between the cash inow and the cash outow. The cash inow is
calculated by summing up the prots due to the seal of the electricity, district
heating and cooling energy. The assessment of these ows is done by multiplying
the net power of the plant by the annual operating hours of the plant, the result
must be multiplied by the energy price, [$/kWh], to obtain the cash inow.
The cost of electricity used in the present investigation is set at 0.28 e/kWh,
while the cost of district heating energy is assumed to be 0.035 e/kWh [62].
Since the absorption technology is new, no data have been found for the price of
the cooling energy; the same price of the district heating energy is hypothesized.
The following relation shows the estimation of the total income due to the energy
sold.
Cash

Operating
Hours × 0.035
In this study the annual hours of operation are set to 7000, meaning that around
two months per year the plant does not work and the ordinary maintenance can
be done. The total investment cost of the plant represents the cash outow at the
year zero, from the rst year the cost of the plant is given by the sum of all the
costs shown in Equations 4.30-4.35. The model for its calculation is taken from
[61]. The incentives are not taken into account in this estimation. The sum of
the capital and the operating costs gives the total cost of the plant. The capital
cost is composed by deprecation cost ( ˙Cdep), maintenance cost ( ˙Cmai), interest
on investment cost ( ˙Cint), insurance cost ( ˙Cins) and taxation cost ( ˙Ctax). These
costs are calculated as shows here below.

4.3
Summary
Software and methods used in the following analysis are introduced in this chap-
ter.
After the development of slightly dierent designs with the component based
simulation tools DNA, a sensitivity analysis was carried out.
Through this
analysis was realised an optimized model for each plant. Finally an economic
analysis of each plant, optimized and not, was conducted.
==PAGE:91==
Chapter 5
Development of Plant Models
This study wants to nd the best eciency design for a trigeneration plant.
The technologies employed in the plant development are introduced in Chapter
3 and listed here below:
 Gasication of municipal solid waste for syngas production.
 Solid oxide fuel cells for electricity production.
 Steam cycle for heat recovery after SOFC plant. Mechanical power and
hot water for district heating are produced through the steam cycle.
 Absorption plant for the production of cold water that could be used for
industrial and civil purposes. After the economizer, the energy content of
the ue gas makes the operation of the chiller possible.
Six plant designs and the corresponding operating conditions are detailed shown
in this chapter. This study concerns, in particular, the solutions with the split
amount of stacks.
All the simulations are run by using the Dynamic Network Analysis (DNA)
software. The analysis is carried out in steady state mode, without taking into
account plant start up and shut down and with the assumption of constant fuel
mass ow.
==PAGE:92==
68
Development of Plant Models
5.1
General Description of the Plant
A simple block diagram of the conguration under study is depicted in Figure
4.1. Municipal solid waste is fuelled to the dryer where the removal of moisture
content from waste occurs. The dried waste enters into the gasier where chem-
ical reactions between fuel and oxidant take place. The products coming out
from the gasier in the simulations done are syngas and ashes. The synthesis gas
is then sent to the SOFC plant while ashes are removed. Before coming to the
fuel cells the synthesis gas has to be cleaned. In particular hydrogen sulphide
can be dangerous for the cells. Low concentration of H2S, ppmv level, absorbed
at active sites of the anode, is enough to inhibit fuel molecule absorption and
aect the reactions [63]. Higher concentrations of sulfur would cause irreversible
damages. The tolerance for sulfur is strongly related to cells operating condi-
tions and fuel composition. After the cleaning, the fuel reaches the SOFC plant
for the electricity production. Since the fuel utilization factor of the cells is not
100%, some of the gas comes out from the anode without having reacted, in
the same way not reacted air comes out from the cathode. These two ows are
introduced in a burner where the combustion occurs. Flue gas from the burner
is used to feed the heat recovery steam generator of a steam cycle. After the
economizer, the gases still have an energetic content that can be used as heat
source for an absorption plant. The nal temperature of the gases outgoing from
the absorption plant is set at 90 , this value is high enough to avoid corrosion
problems.
The number of stacks in the study is set at 30000. By estimating that the di-
mension of a stack is 12 × 12 × 12cm the volume occupied by 30000 stacks is
about 52 m3, although, additional space is needed for the insulation.
In reference to [28], the congurations with and without the use of hybrid re-
cuperator are studied. Moreover, the possibility of splitting the total amount
of SOFCs is evaluated. Referring to [14], all the dierent plant congurations
(without hybrid recuperator, with hybrid recuperator and with hybrid recuper-
ator and the split amount of stacks) are investigated either by using an anode
pre-heater or a methanator before the anode. With respect to solutions with two
stack blocks, dierent designs are developed for anode pre-heater and methana-
tor respectively. It is necessary to make the simulations of the plant possible.
Fuel Composition
The performances of the plant are closely related to the fuel composition. As
it is shown in Chapter 2, it is hard to dene the composition of MSW. Many
factors like season, region, income level and other high variable elements aect
the waste composition [27].

Design)

5.2
Integrated Gasication, SOFCs, Steam Cycle
and Absorption Chiller Plant with and with-
out the use of Hybrid Recuperator (Anode
Pre-Heater Design)
In this section the design of the trigeneration plant without hybrid recuperator
is described. The performances of the plant are also analysed after the introduc-
tion of this heat exchanger. The component is a simple heat exchanger that, as
illustrated in [28] and proved from results obtained in the present investigation,
increases the performance of the plant without excessive cost.
Plant Description
A draw of the plant without the hybrid recuperator is shown in Figure 5.1.
==PAGE:94==
70
Development of Plant Models
Figure 5.1: Plant schema with anode pre-heater and without hybrid recuper-
ator.
==PAGE:95==
5.2 Integrated Gasication, SOFCs, Steam Cycle and Absorption Chiller
Plant with and without the use of Hybrid Recuperator (Anode Pre-Heater
Design)
71
Stream 1 of MSW is introduced into the dryer before reaching the gasier. Part
of the water content removed from fuel is mixed with hot air in the mixer, the
mixture is used as oxidant in the gasier. The other part of the water removed
from waste, current number 14, is heated and used to feed the dryer.
The
temperature of ow 15 is set at 200  to allow proper operation of the dryer.
3 kg/s, equal to 10.8 ton/h, is the mass ow of MSW incoming to the plant at
ambient temperature (15 ) and atmospheric pressure (1.01325 bar). The high
size of the plant could avoid problems of frequent start up and shut down, this
matter is of primary importance for small scale plants. The water content of
waste is reduced after the dryer and the temperature of the current entering the
gasier (ow 2) is set to 150 . The fuel and the oxidant are introduced into
the gasier with currents 2 and 13 respectively. There is no needed to introduce
steam with stream 98 for the operation of the reactor. The ashes are eliminated
through ow 99 while syngas is used to pre-heat the air before the mixer and
also the steam used into the dryer.
After having used part of the energy content of the syngas, it is cleaned into the
gas cleaner to satisfy the strict SOFCs cleanliness requirements. The removal
eciency of the cleaner is theoretically set to 1, meaning that all the hydrogen
sulphide present in the ow is theoretically removed through the current 97.
However, the literature shows that a very low concentration of H2S does not
aect the operating condition of the cells [63].
After the desulfurizer, the syngas passes through the anode pre-heater (AP)
before going to the SOFCs anode. On the other side the air is compressed and
pre-heated in the cathode pre-heater (CP) before coming to the cathode. The
reactions occurring into the cells allow to produce direct current, it needs to
be converted in alternating current by using a converter. The o-gas outgoing
from SOFCs is used in the anode pre-heater, it heats the fuel at a temperature
high enough to avoid problem into the cells. The same happens on the cathode
side, here the hot uid is o-air coming out from SOFCs and the cold uid is air
from the air blower. The operating temperature of SOFCs in this chapter is set
at 780 ; temperatures of inlet fuel and air are respectively set at 600  and
650 . These values can be lower than the operating temperature thanks to the
exothermic reactions occurring in the cells. Since the cathode is thicker than
the anode, the dierence between SOFCs working temperature and incoming
ow temperature is higher for the air than for the fuel. The two blowers before
the SOFC plant, air blower and MSW-gas blower, are necessary to overcome
only the pressure losses along the way.
After the heat exchangers the streams of fuel and air are introduced into a
burner for the combustion. The combustion products are used to feed the heat
recovery steam generator of a steam cycle. The energy content of the o-gas is
then used to feed an absorption plant that produces water at 4 .
A heat exchanger is used instead of the condenser in the DNA code for the
single stage steam cycle. This helps the district heating (DH) simulation for the
production of hot water. Cold water used to cool down the outgoing gas from
==PAGE:96==
72
Development of Plant Models
the steam turbine has a temperature of 50 , while the temperature of the hot
water used for the district heating network is 80 . No auxiliary condenser is
designed in the congurations investigated. The steam energy content after the
steam turbine is fully used for district heating network.
The ue gas coming out from the economizer provides the energy at the desorber
of the absorption plant before going to the chimney.
Plant Data
As already mentioned the ow of MSW introduced into the plant is 3 kg/s,
after the dryer the ow rate of dried waste is 2.86 kg/s.
The mass ow of
syngas outgoing from the gasier is 5.61 kg/s. Since the content of H2S in the
synthesis gas is low, the quantity of syngas reaching the cells is still 5.61 kg/s.
The electricity production of the SOFC plant in this case is around 20.33 MW.
The eciency of the fuel cells plant is evaluated through the following relation.
ηSOF Cs = Net
Power
from

Fuel
Consumption[kW]
(5.1)
In the conguration of the plant actually under investigation, the combustion
occurs in the burner and the temperature of the products reaches 489 . The
energy content is used to produce steam at a temperature of about 459  and a
pressure of 60 bar, the steam is then introduced into the steam turbine. The me-
chanical power produced by the steam cycle is about 5.93 MW and the eciency
of the cycle is evaluated as
ηSteamCycle =

(5.2)
The thermal power available for the district heating is 15.48 MW. In this condi-

the power available for district heating and energy introduced into the plant by
the fuel (MSW), as shown in Equation 5.3.
ηDH = Thermal
Power
available
for
District

(5.3)
After the economizer the combustion products still have high temperature, close
to 220 , and it is exploited in the absorption plant. The cold water produced
==PAGE:97==
5.2 Integrated Gasication, SOFCs, Steam Cycle and Absorption Chiller
Plant with and without the use of Hybrid Recuperator (Anode Pre-Heater

73
could be used, for example, for district cooling.
As shown in the following
equation, the coecient of performance of an absorption chiller is dened as
the ratio between the cooling output from the evaporator and the required heat
input.
COP = Cooling
Power[kW]
Heat
Input[kW]
(5.4)
Through the previous denition, the COP of the absorption plant under inves-
tigation is around 0.617. Usually absorption plant COP is higher, the value
obtained in this study is suitable for the trigenertion design. The advantage, in
this case, is given by the recovery of heat that otherwise would be thrown away.
The cooling power obtained with this conguration is around 6 MW, as term of
reference it is possible to consider that the daily household consumption for air
conditioner is around 5 kW [64]. The large amount of cooling power produced
requires to nd appropriate power consumers.
Rokni investigates in [28] the possibility of recovering heat in the hybrid recu-
perator (HR). The energy content of the ue gas after the economizer can be
used to pre-heat the air ow before the cathode pre-heater, the heat exchanger
in which this occurs is called hybrid recuperator. The energy recovered in the
HR is subtracted to the absorption plant and, because of this, the mass ow of
lithium bromide circulating in the chiller is strongly reduced, from 33.34 kg/s
to 1.38 kg/s. This is essentially due to the reduction of temperature before the
desorber, from about 220  to about 95 . On the base of heat source temper-
ature, the absorption plant model implemented in DNA allows lithium bromide
ow rate changing. Higher temperature of current 60 implies a higher mass
ow of lithium bromide circulating into the chiller. The reduction of lithium
bromide mass ow in the absorption chiller leads to a drop of cooling power,
from about 6 MW to 243 kW. This strongly aects the cooling capacity of the
plant. Nevertheless, few hundred kW of cooling power are enough to be used for
civil purposes and also for some small industrial application. As expected from
the DNA model of absorption chiller, the COP is not aected by the reduction
of heat source temperature.
A draw of the plant conguration with the hybrid recuperator is illustrated in
Figure 5.2. In order to have a temperature high enough to let the absorption
plant run, the minimum temperature dierence for HR is set to 38 .

With the introduction of one more heat exchanger, the hybrid recuperator, the
total thermal eciency (LHV) of the plant increases by about 5 percentage
points, from 44.16% to 49.79%. The electric power production is slightly en-
hanced compared to the previous conguration. Even the power available for
district heating grows and reaches 21.88 MW. The district heating eciency is
improved by about 12 percentage points.
The introduction of hybrid recuperator reduces the heat exchange at the cath-
ode pre-heater, hotter air reaches the burner and hotter combustion products
are used for the steam cycle operation. A greater steam mass ow can be in-
troduced into the steam turbine and more mechanical power is produced. As
a result of higher steam ow rate, hot water produced for district heating in-
creases.
Main input data used for both plants of Figure 5.1 and Figure 5.2 are summa-
rized in Table 5.2.
DNA results for solutions described in this section are given in Table 5.3 for the
plant without hybrid recuperator and in Table 5.4 for the second conguration
described in the paragraph.
The comparison of Table 5.3 and Table 5.4 shows that the total power production
of design without hybrid recuperator is around 3 MW lower than in the other
case; the total power consumption is decreased only 200 kW. This is also due to
the reduction of lithium bromide mass ow in the absorption chiller, it reduces
the auxiliary consumption. The introduction of hybrid recuperator brings about
an increase in steam cycle and district heating eciencies, while a reduction of
SOFC plant eciency is observed. This lower value of SOFCs eciency is due
to the denition of the parameter as expressed in Equation 5.5.
ηSOF Cs =
Net
Power
from
SOFCs[kW]
Fuel
Consumption[kW] + Recuperated
Heat[kW]
(5.5)
The thermal eciency is higher than that reached with integrated gasication
combined cycle (IGCC), it is actually around 40% [65].
The denition of the plant eciency used in DNA does not take into account
thermal and cooling power production. High values of district heating eciency
and COP are appreciated to better use the energy content of the fuel provided
to the plant. In the present study the values of these two parameters are indi-
cated apart from the plant eciency for each design.
It is interesting to observe as, the temperature and quantity of heat exchanged
in the heat recovery steam generator increase by introducing the hybrid recu-
perator. Figure 5.3 shows those eects.

Since in both cases the temperature of the ow 22 is much higher than 650 ,
there is no need of introducing one more heat exchanger after the methanator.
This high temperature ow can be directly introduced into the SOFCs anode.
Plant Data
In this conguration the main parameters of the plant are unchanged but the
anode side inlet temperature is not set at 650 . The reforming process, that
occurs into the methanator is exothermic; because of this, the temperature of
the ow after the component is increased. Other input data for the plant are
the same of Table 5.2. The unvaried data allow to see better the inuence of
mathanator introduction on plant operation.
The methanator makes possible to reach three times higher content of methane
in the ow. The methane amount in the synthesis gas is very low and the electric
power produced by SOFCs is not signicantly aected by this parameter. The
fuel that comes out from the SOFCs without reacting, ow 23, is burned into
the burner with the air coming out from the cathode pre-heater, current 29. The
fuel introduced in the burner has a higher temperature than that reached with
anode pre-heater design; no heat recovery is performed between the stream
coming out from SOFCs anode and the burner.
The eect is an increased
combustion temperature and therefore ue gas temperature resulted higher. It
brings about to have a higher turbine inlet temperature and higher steam mass
ow circulating into the steam cycle. The mechanical power production turns
out to be bigger. The thermal power available for district heating is increased
of about 1 MW, around 16.9 MW.
The increase of methane content results in more internal reforming into SOFCs
and less air is required to cool the cells, the consequence is the decrease of air
blower workload.
Flue gas temperature after the economizer is high enough to have a notable
mass ow of the lithium bromide solution into the absorption chiller, 27.54
kg/s. This ow rate is lower than in the plant of Figure 5.1 and accordingly
the cooling power produced is lower, about 4.85 MW. The temperature of the
current coming out from the economizer depends on dierent factors, among
the others the gas mass ow and temperature are of paramount importance. As
expected, referring to the Equation 5.4, the COP of the plant is not aected by
the temperature at the desorber. Its value is unchanged and equal to 0.617.
Thanks to the introduction of the mathanator the thermal eciency of the plant
increases from 44.16% to 46.17%. Therefore, from the thermodynamic point of
view, the solution with the methanator turns out to be better. Due to the fact
that the net thermal eciency of the plant is evaluated by Equation 4.28, the
improvement reached is basically due to the higher mechanical power resulting
from steam cycle. It must be remembered that the solution just studied also
requires less power consumption.

As already observed in the plant with anode pre-heater, the energy content of
ue gas after the heat recovery steam generator can be used in the hybrid recu-
perator [28] before feeding the absorption chiller. A draw of the plant is shown
in Figure 5.5. Input data of this plant are the same of the plant without hybrid
recuperator, only one little change is made to let the plant work: the minimum
dierence temperature at the hybrid recuperator is set at 36 . With this con-
dition it is possible to have an energy content capable of feeding the absorption
chiller. The reduction of 2  of the minimum temperature dierence allows to
recover more heat, this contributes to the plant eciency improvement.
The rst observation done with this conguration is that the thermal eciency
(LHV) increases by about 4 percentage points, from 46.17% to 50.99%. This
eciency increment is lower than the one reached in the plant with the anode
pre-heater because the increase of net power produced is lower.
With the use of the hybrid recuperator, the mechanical power produced by the
steam cycle increases while the electric power produced by SOFCs is almost un-
changed compared to the plant without heat exchanger concerned. The growth
of power production is combined with the higher request of power for the aux-
iliary.

pre-heater, the cooling power drops strongly, for the plant of Figure 5.5 it is
146.3 kW. The calculation of the COP through the Equation 5.4 gives back
a COP of 0.618, as expected from DNA absorption chiller model this value is
almost unchanged. Only the cooling power production is interested by the tem-
perature change of the heat source.
With regard to district heating potentiality, it is possible to see that this is
increased of about 5 MW compared to the solution without hybrid recuperator,
the total production is equal to 21.97 MW.

5.4
Integrated Gasication, SOFCs, Steam Cycle
and Absorption Chiller Plant with two blocks
of SOFC stacks (Anode Pre-Heater Design)
In this section the plant illustrated in Figure 5.7 is analysed. This conguration
with the split amount of SOFCs is introduced, investigated and compared with
the previous solutions.
Plant Description
After having seen, as expected, that the performances of the plant increase with
the introduction of the hybrid recuperator, the thermodynamics of the plant
with the split amount of SOFCs is studied. The 30000 stacks were divided in
two blocks.
Figure 5.7 shows the plant design studied in this paragraph. Design changes
made concern the SOFC plant. The amount of cells is split in two dierent
blocks of stacks, they have dierent number of cells and operating conditions.
It is possible to use the o-gas after the rst block of stacks in the anode pre-
heater to pre-heat the fuel.
The temperature of the o-fuel after the anode
pre-heater is still high enough and can feed the second block. It is not possible
to do a similar recovery at the cathode side, by using the ow 28 in the cath-
ode pre-heater the temperature would decrease too much and the stream could
not be used in the second block. The investigation of the plant introduced in
this chapter is done by letting the second stack block operate at 800 . These
temperature is chosen for a good operation of the plant without any signicant
changes of other input data. The temperature at the anode side is a little bit
low, but it does not give any theoretical problem of operation. Since the o-air is
directly introduced into the second block of stacks with a temperature of 780 ,
the cells have to operate at higher temperature than the rst block, 800 . This
value is also suitable for the plant investigated in the next paragraph, and it is
chosen here for a better comparison of performance.
In order to let the electrochemical reactions occur in the second block of stacks,
the fuel utilization factor of the rst block does not have to be too high. Con-
cerning the number of cells, it was decided to use a bigger amount in the rst
block of stacks that operates at lower temperature. In fact, the cell price is
related to the operating temperature and it rises with the temperature. Fur-
thermore, the electric power production increases by using cells operating at
lower temperature.

and mass ow also the mechanical power at the steam turbine decreases. Like-

that of the plant without the split amount of stacks. In the plant under study
in this section the thermal power obtained is around 19.203 MW.

kW, it is not much dierent from that obtained from the plant of Figure 5.2.

a considerable changing.

the temperature of the currents too much by preventing the streams use in the
second block.

burner is used at the cathode pre-heater to pre-heat the air. In this congura-
tion the energy content of ow 40 is high enough to pre-heat the air and then go
to the heat recovery steam generator of the steam cycle. A solution that consid-
ers the recovery of the energy content of ow 39 into the cathode pre-heater was
implemented without success. The lower air ow rate, due to the methanator,
did not allow to provide the energy required to pre-heat the air in the cathode
pre heater and then feed the burner.

Plant Data
The results obtained with the program show that, by splitting the total amount
of stacks in two blocks the thermal eciency (LHV) increases from 50.99% to
52.61%. As in the previous paragraph, also here, the only change is done in the
SOFC plant.
From the analysis of the SOFC plant, it is possible to see that the total electric
power produced is about 23.91 MW, 19.91 MW from the rst block of stacks
and about 4 MW from the second block. The total electric power production
in this case is about 3.6 MW higher compared to the plant with only one block
of stacks, while the total power consumption is only around 400 kW higher. In
particular, the workload of the air blower increases because more air has to be
fed to SOFCs to cool them down.
In this conguration in series, both currents going to the burner have the same
temperature, 800 . This situation leads to reach a higher temperature after
the burner, the energy content could be used in both the cathode pre-heater
and later in the heat recovery steam generator.
The temperature after the
burner is around 900  while the temperature after the cathode pre-heater is
around 564 . This last value is lower than the one obtained from the plant
with only one block of stacks, this causes the lower turbine inlet temperature.
The reduction of steam mass ow, due to the lower temperature of ue gas
entering the heat recovery steam generator, causes the drop of mechanical power
produced by the steam turbine. The lower energy content in the current going
out from the turbine reduces the thermal power available for district heating,
from about 21.97 MW, reached in the conguration with one block of stacks, to
about 18.20 MW, found in the conguration investigated in this section.
It has to be noticed that the cooling power in for this solution is higher than
in the plant with only one block of SOFC stacks, approximately 220.3 kW are
reached. The COP value, obtained through the denition of Equation 5.4, is
0.617 as expected.

5.14, it can be observed that the emissions are not substantially aected by
methanator introduction.
It should not be forgotten that, also in this case, the content of methane in
the syngas current after methanator is about three times higher. Although the
total methane content is still very low, this increase encourages the internal
reforming of SOFCs and less air is required to cool down the system, this leads
to a reduction of air blower workload.

5.6
Summary
Six dierent congurations of an integrated gasication, SOFCs, steam cycle
and absorption chiller plant for trigenartion of electricity, heating and cooling
are studied.
The basic idea of the conguration is illustrated in Figure 4.1. After the evi-
dence of the eciency growth, obtained by introducing the hybrid recuperator,
==PAGE:120==
96
Development of Plant Models
Figure 5.10: T −∆Q diagram of heat recovery steam generator. The hot uid
is ue gas and the cold uid is steam circulating into the steam
cycle.
the solutions with the split amount of stacks are developed and analysed. By
splitting the total amount of SOFCs in two blocks, operating under dierent
conditions, it was necessary to change the disposition of the components to let
the plant work during the simulations. The anode pre-heater solution with two
blocks of stacks shows slight higher eciency than the methanator design. This
last solution allows a lower energy recovery.
Due to the dierences in congurations, the minimum temperature dierence at
the super-heater are slightly dierent, but always included in the range between
30 and 35 . Temperature dierences lower than 30  are not evaluated to
limit costs and dimensions of the heat exchanger. It is necessary to remark one
more aspect about the heat recovery steam generator, in particular regarding
the evaporator. The temperature in the evaporator should be theoretically con-
stant, in practice it is possible to have a temperature dierence of few degrees
due to thermal losses. Congurations with anode pre-heater show a higher tem-
perature dierence compared to those observed in the methanator solutions.
The parameters and the conditions imposed for the steam cycle guarantee a
vapour quality high enough to avoid excessive corrosion problems for steam tur-
bine blades.
The congurations with two blocks of stacks can produce more electric power
==PAGE:121==
5.6 Summary
97
and show better thermal eciencies (LHV) than those with only one block. In
Table 5.15 are summarized the main results obtained for the dierent plants.
The simulations of plant designs investigated are run by using similar operating
conditions. The aim is to see which design, among those studied, could be the
most promising. By comparing results in Table 5.15, it is possible to observe
that the highest thermal eciencies, evaluated as the ratio between the net
power production and the total fuel consumption, are reached for solutions with
two blocks of stacks. The crucial point of this chapter is that, either adopting
anode pre-heater or methanator conguration, the solutions with two blocks of
stacks allow to achieve higher plant eciency. The dierent operating condi-
tions do not excessively increase the plant price.
For waste-red district heating plant exists a simple rule of thumb for the cal-
culation of energy recovered [44]: from 1 tonne of waste could be obtained
around 2 MWh of heat and 2-3 MWh of electricity. The plant investigated us-
ing waste gasication, but the power production can be considered include in
the expected range. Only for the plant without hybrid reuperator low values of
heat are shown.

Chapter 6
Model Optimization
All the plants designed are studied in Chapter 5 without signicant changes in
input data. It allows to compare them under similar operating conditions. The
following step of the project is the optimization of all the trigeneration plant
solutions investigated in the previous chapter. The maximization of thermal
eciency (LHV) was the purpose of the process. Only SOFC plant parameters
were studied. In particular, values of SOFCs operating temperature, SOFCs
fuel utilization factor and number of stacks with the plant were analysed in the
sensitivity analysis.
6.1
Parameters of the Sensitivity Analysis
The design of each plant has been investigated in detail in Chapter 5. The atten-
tion is now focused on the SOFC plant, it is the top plant in the congurations
under study. The theoretical changes in the plant behaviour are investigated by
modifying SOFCs parameters. Simulations with dierent values of SOFCs fuel
utilization factor (Uf), SOFCs operating temperature and number of stacks are
carried out with the software. Dierent thermal eciency trends are observed
by varying SOFCs parameters in the plant. The analysis of the plants with two
blocks of stacks is carried out by changing separately the parameters of the two
blocks.
The eects on the trigeneration plant are dierent from those observed on the
SOFC plant. Consequences for the fuel cell plant are summarized here:
==PAGE:124==
100
Model Optimization
 SOFCs operating temperature does not aect the current density.
By
increasing the temperature, the Nernst voltage decreases while the loss
due to polarization factors increases. It leads to have lower cell voltage
and, consequently, lower stack voltage.
 The current density decreases with the fuel utilization factor. The Nernst
voltage increases and the polarization loss term lessens. Higher values of
cell and stack voltage are reached.
 The increase of stack number does not substantially aect the current den-
sity and the Nernst voltage, but a decrease in polarization loss is observed.
This fact brings about cell and stack voltage increase.
It was observed that in some of the cases under study the parameter that mainly
inuences the eciency of the plant is the fuel utilization factor of the cells. Usu-
ally this value varies between 0.5 and 0.95 [66]. In the sensitivity analysis this
factor is changed in a wider range, the lowest theoretical value chosen is the
last one that allows the correct plant operation. The limit of the fuel utilization
factor for the optimization was chosen to be 0.5, even if lower Uf would allow
to reach higher performances. Including also new technology goals, that aim for
reaching lower operating temperatures and decreasing material costs, the cells
temperature was varied between 650 and 900  during the simulations. The
maximum amount of cells simulated is set at 300000, but this value is not taken
into consideration for any of the optimized designs.
The analysis of plants with two blocks of stacks shows that the eciency is more
aected by the parameters of the rst block, it may be due to the higher number
of stacks used in it.
After having studied the eciency trends by varying separately SOFCs param-
eters, one of the most performing values of the most aecting parameter is set.
Further simulations are carried out by changing other factors. Optimized so-
lutions in terms of thermal eciency (LHV) are found. It is proven that the
solutions with the split amount of stacks can reach better performances than
other congurations.

has been possible to simulate a high number of plant working points.

the reduction of both fuel utilization factor and operating temperature of the

The growth of the percentage of fuel used in SOFC plant increases the power
produced by SOFCs but, at the same time, it is necessary to supply more air at
the cathode side to let the reactions occurring in the cells. The higher air mass
ow leads to an increase of the air blower workload. Higher ow rate introduced
with the air blower aects the burner operation. The increase of air amount
going to the burner with low temperature causes the combustion temperature
reduction; consequently, the heat available for the steam cycle decreases. This
temperature drop brings about the steam mass ow reduction in the steam
cycle, it is also followed by the reduction of mechanical power produced by the
steam cycle. Also the district heating production is aected by the steam mass
==PAGE:127==
6.2 Optimization of Anode Pre-Heater and Methanator congurations
without Hybrid Recuperator
103
ow reduction. High values of fuel utilization factor provoke the decrease of
the heat recovered in the heat recovery steam generator, it is due to the lower
energy content of the ue gas. Since this conguration does not have the hybrid
recuperator, all the enthalpy content after the steam cycle is available for the
absorption chiller, a growth of cooling power produced is observed. The eects
of the increased fuel utilization factor are total power production reduction and
total power consumption increase, the result is a lower thermal eciency of
the plant. The reduction of Uf causes the drop of electricity produced from
SOFCs cycle, this is counterbalanced by power saved at the air blower and by
the increase of mechanical power at the steam turbine, the resulting eect is an
increase in thermal eciency.
The change of Uf has eects on the compositions of the o-gas from SOFCs and
on the ue gas coming out the burner. These variations on o-fuel are shown
in Table 6.1.

Data of Table 6.1 show how the decrease of the fuel utilization factor leads to
a reduction of hydrogen and water in the o-fuel, while a bigger quantity of
carbon monoxide and carbon dioxide not reacted is found. Table 6.2 exhibits
the eects on the ue gas after the combustion process.
With a lower fuel
utilization factor, it is possible to observe higher quantity of carbon dioxide and
water in the ue gas. Observations just done can be considered valid also for
methanator conguration.
The rst impact of the higher operating temperature of the cells can be seen in a
lower electric power production of the SOFC plant. It has to be reminded that by
increasing the operating temperature the activation losses decrease and higher
cell eciency is reached. Besides that, other problems like the decrease of volt-
age, corrosion and electrolyte evaporation occur. The change of the operating
temperature aects also the heat recovery at the anode and cathode pre-heaters
and the workload of the air blower. The operation at high temperature leads the
need to introduce more air into the cells to cool down the system. Moreover, the

mechanical power consumed from the air blower increases. The operating con-
ditions of the steam plant and of the absorption chiller are not strongly aected
by the dierent SOFCs temperatures. The global result of the increased SOFCs
operating temperature is the reduction of the total power produced, mainly due
to the drop of SOFCs electric power, and the total power consumption growth.
The excessive lowering of fuel cells temperature shows slightly higher power con-
sumption and lower power production, the consequences for the plant thermal
eciency are observed in Figure 6.1. The change of the SOFCs temperature has
to be combined with the variation of the temperatures of the inlet SOFCs ows
at the anode and the cathode. Lack of SOFCs data causes the assumption of
the same reduction in inlet ows and SOFCs temperature.
A major amount of SOFCs allows to obtain higher electric power production.
By increasing the number of stacks, without changing the fuel mass ow, brings
about a lower amount of fuel per stack. It is mainly due to slower increase in
electric power produced by SOFCs. By decreasing the fuel per cell the ionic
concentration is reduced below its limit. The result is the reduction of specic
power production and the positive eect of more stacks used diminishes. The
opposite problem is observed by reducing too much the number of stacks: the
amount of fuel per stack increases and the ionic concentration reaches its upper
limit. In Figure 6.2 it is possible to see that, after a sudden eciency improve-
ment obtained by raising the number of stacks from 30000 to 100000, a minor
advantage is observed by using a bigger amount of stacks.
The inuence of
more stacks on the plant cost has also to be considered. Light dierences are
observed in steam cycle and absorption chiller operation. The global eect of a
bigger amount of cells is an increase of the eciency, especially due to the major
production of electricity. With 300000 cells the eciency reaches the value of
46%, changes on utilization factor and on operating temperature lead to higher
eciency levels.
The rst parameter set to nd the optimum operating point is the utilization
factor. This factor is set at 0.5, the corresponding thermal eciency is 47.67%.
Further simulations by changing the SOFCs operating temperature are run and
==PAGE:129==

without Hybrid Recuperator

the results show optimum conditions for an SOFCs temperature of 690 . The
last parameter investigated was the number of SOFC stacks, by increasing the
stack number of 10000 units the eciency growth is 0.35 percentage points.
Due to the high SOFCs price a good thermodynamic and economic compromise
could be found in the solution with 30000 stacks. For the plant under investi-
gation the maximum thermal eciency is equal to 48.8% and it is reached by
simulating the following SOFCs operating conditions:
 Utilization factor = 0.5
 SOFCs operating temperature = 690 
 Number of stacks = 30000.

while the cell voltage increases from 0.7897 up to 0.9050 V.

 The hybrid recuperator introduction increases the complexity of the plant.
==PAGE:135==
6.3 Optimization of Anode Pre-Heater Conguration with Hybrid
Recuperator
111
Because of this, fewer plant working conditions can be simulated with the
software.
 In the solution studied in this paragraph, the SOFCs operating tempera-
ture aects the thermal eciency more than the utilization factor.
The thermal eciency trend, obtained by changing the SOFCs working tem-
perature, is not really dierent from the trend seen in the plant without hybrid
recuperator. As already seen the temperature reduction increases the cell elec-
tricity production and reduces the air blower workload. Steam cycle and ab-
sorption plant are not strongly aected by the reduction of the SOFCs working
temperature. The global eect provoked by the drop of this parameter on the
plant is the thermal eciency increase.
The impact of the fuel utilization factor and temperature on the plant is the
same already observed in the previous section. The combination of hybrid re-
cuperator introduction and SOFCs lowered operating temperature leads to the
reduction heat exchanged in the anode pre-heater. Higher ue gas temperature
is reached and power production of the steam cycle increases.
Figure 6.7 shows the inuence of the number of stacks on the plant eciency.
Despite less simulation were carried out, it is possible to see that the trend is
not much dierent from that already observed in the previous cases.
The temperature is the most aecting parameter for this design, its value is
set at 660  and further simulations are carried out by changing the utilization
factor. Figure 6.8 shows the results of the simulations.
It can be noticed that the thermal eciency decreases for utilization factor
lower than 0.655. The increase of fuel reacting into the stacks leads the growth
of electric power produced, while more air is necessary at the cathode side to let
the reactions occur. The big quantity of air lowers the combustion temperature
and this has an impact on the steam cycle: mechanical power and district
heating production decrease. Furthermore, the air blower workload increases.
Very low values of the fuel utilization factor bring about a reduction of electricity
produced, the advantages led to the steam cycle can not be compensated any
more. Working at lower temperature less air is necessary to cool down the stacks
and the advantage in decreasing Uf reduces its eect. The excessive reduction
of the fuel utilization factor, when the plant works at low temperature, leads a
decrease of the thermal eciency.
It is observed that, by decreasing SOFCs operating temperature the drop of the
fuel utilization factor has a major importance. A maximum of eciency for an
utilization factor equal to 0.665 is found.
In this case, the increase of stack number from 30000 to 90000 brings about an
eciency improvement of two points percentage.

6.5 Optimization of Anode Pre-Heater Conguration with Hybrid

117
taking into account the economical aspect, the optimized solution for this plant
was designed with 30000 stacks. The optimization of this plant gives back an
eciency of 52.19% with the use of the following parameters:
 SOFCs operating temperature = 740 
 Utilization factor = 0.530
 Number of stacks = 30000.

while the cell voltage increases from 0.7897 up to 0.8873 V.

==PAGE:143==
6.5 Optimization of Anode Pre-Heater Conguration with Hybrid
Recuperator and the split amount of SOFCs
119
The eciency reached with this plant is higher than that observed for previous
solutions. The plant eciency is mainly aected by fuel utilization factor of the
rst block of stacks, Uf1. The minimum value chosen for this parameter in this
study is 0.5. In this particular conguration, it must be considered that high
values of Uf1 will prevent the sucient fuel ow at the second block of stacks.
By lowering Uf1 and keeping constant the fuel utilization factor of the second
block of SOFCs, Uf2, the power produced by the rst block decreases, while the
production of the second block increases. Since the rst block is characterised
by higher amount of stacks, the inuence of Uf1 on the plant is stronger than
that of Uf2. Bigger quantity of air is required by working with two blocks of
stacks, it reduces combustion and ue gas temperatures, while the ue gas ow
rate increases. Whereas the lower temperature tends to decrease the steam mass
ow, the higher ow rate tends to increase the steam circulating into the steam
cycle. The mechanical power produced is related to the steam ow rate.
With regard to SOFCs operating temperature, it has to be noticed that few
values allow the operation of the plant without producing problems. The second
block of stacks is substantially not aected from the operating temperature of
the rst block. Lower SOFCs temperature leads to require colder air at the
cathode side, the o-air coming to the burner is hotter and the temperature of
ue gas is higher.
Uf2 aects plant eciency more than the operating temperature of the second
block of stacks. This last parameter does not aect the rst block operation.
The eect of Uf2 on plant operation has the same trend observed for Uf1. The
lower inuence of Uf2 on the plant eciency is due to the lower stack number
of the second block. High values of the fuel utilization factor stop the electricity
production at the second block of stacks. It is due to the higher fuel ow rate
in the stacks, it increases the ionic concentration up to its upper limit. When
the limit is achieved the electricity production stops.
In Figure 6.12 it is possible to see the inuence of higher number of stacks. The
tendency is the same observed for other plants. The advantage obtained by
increasing the number of stacks of the rst block is higher than that achievable
by enlarging the number of stacks in the second block. This fact could be due
to the lower SOFCs operating temperature. Cells working at lower temperature
produce more electricity and, therefore, they have more inuence on the total
plant eciency.
A plant eciency of 57.86% is achieved by simulating the following parameters:
 Utilization factor (rst block) = 0.500
 SOFCs (rst block) operating temperature = 700 
 SOFCs (second block) operating temperature = 790 

==PAGE:149==

introducing the hybrid recuperator.
The SOFCs operating temperature that maximises the thermal eciency is
lower for anode pre-heater than for methanator congurations. The amount of
air necessary in the second case is lower than that required for the operation
with anode pre-heater. This could be partially due to the composition of the
syngas. In the anode pre-heater conguration the hydrogen content is higher
and more air is required to let the reactions occur into the cells. The workload
of the air blower increases. No signicant changes are observed in terms of heat
exchange at the cathode pre-heater. The strong inuence of SOFCs operating
temperature on o-fuel temperature is more evident in methanator solutions.
The optimizations allow to increase the total power production of the plant
while they reduce the power consumption. Good potentiality were observed for
congurations with split amount of stacks. For those congurations the increase
of thermal eciency is about 5 and 6 percentage points, compared to the values
of Chapter 5, for anode pre-heater and methanator solution respectively.

Chapter 7
Economic Analysis
This chapter concerns the economic analysis of dierent plant designs.
The
study is carried out by developing a model in Microsoft Excel©, this model
allows to calculate the purchase equipment cost and the additional cost of each
component. The method for cost calculation is detailed explained in Chapter
4. The total investment cost of each element is obtained by summing up the
two aforementioned costs. The prices of all components constituting the plant
are added together and an approximate evaluation of the total investment cost
is obtained. An estimate of the net present value (NPV) is also shown. The
results achieved are shown and discussed here. In this chapter the optimized
operating conditions must be considered as circumstances that maximised the
thermal eciency of the plant.
7.1
Payback Time of Plants with Similar Oper-
ating Conditions
In Chapter 5 are shown dierent plant solutions operating under similar con-
ditions. In this section the same congurations are economically analysed in
terms of NPV and payback time. Figure 7.1 shows the results obtained. Even if
the cost of the methanator is not negligible, it does not strongly aect the total
investment cost. Similar trends are observed for all the cases. Good results are
achieved in terms of benets after twenty years, in particular for solutions with
two blocks of stacks.
The payback time range for cogeneration plants is between two and ten years
==PAGE:152==
128
Economic Analysis
[67]. All the solutions of this study are in accordance with these data and allow
to payback the initial investment between three and ve years.
Figure 7.1: This graphic shows the results for dierent plant designs investi-
gated in this study and working under similar conditions. They
are obtained by implementing the model described in Chapter 4.
The payback time of each plant is given by the intersection of the
NPV line evolution with the coordinate axis.
The starting total investment cost is around 200 million dollars for all the plants
under study. The most expansive solution is the one with anode pre-heater and
hybrid recuperator, this conguration is characterized by the longest payback
time, more than 4 years. The total investment cost of the plant without hybrid
recuperator is lower, but the benet after 20 years is also smaller. It is possible
to see an analogous behaviour by comparing the methanator design with and
without hybrid recuperator. In this last case the payback time of the two solu-
tions is around 4 years, it can be also observed the higher prot obtained after
20 years introducing the hybrid recuperator. Moreover, it must be remembered
that the plant with hybrid recuperator reaches a higher thermal eciency. It
has to be highlighted as the introduction of the this heat exchanger strongly
reduce the cooling capacity of the absorption chiller, this happens either with
one and with two stack blocks. This means that the size of the absorption plant
is smaller and consequently the price is lower.
Figure 7.1 shows that, by considering similar operating conditions for all the con-
gurations studied, the methanator conguration with split amount of SOFCs
is the most convenient. Higher values of the net power production aect the

economic advantages achievable after 20 years. The introduction of the hybrid
recuperator allows to increase the net power of about 3 MW, by splitting the
stacks amount 2 more MW are produced. The comparison with the solution
without hybrid recuperator shows that the net power production increases of 5
MW by introducing the heat exchanger and splitting the stacks in two blocks.
Since thermal power and cooling power are supposed to be sold at the same
price and their sum does not change a lot from one design to the other, these
factor should not strongly aect the results obtained.

Summary
It is possible to conclude that the most performing solutions, in terms of thermal
eciency, could also be interesting from an economic point of view. In partic-

to be not much more expensive than the others. Furthermore, the optimized
solutions of these congurations are also more protable.
==PAGE:159==
Chapter 8
Conclusions
The target of this study was to analyse the possibility of electric, heating and
cooling trigeneration.
Trigeneration allows to recover more energy and reduce the wasted energy.
Waste to Energy technology is demonstrated to be an essential component of a
good waste management solution. Gasication of waste allows to reach high ef-
ciency with a zero-cost fuel. The use of waste for energy production instead of
landll has a positive impact on the environment. The economic sustainability
of the technology was evaluated and good results were obtained also from this
point of view.
Therefore, the technology studied combines benets in terms of eciency and
pollution with an economically competitive solution.
Integration of gasier, solid oxide fuel cells and steam cycle was already investi-
gated in literature. This study combined these technologies with an absorption
chiller. The theoretical operation of the trigeneration plant is simulated.
It focused on nding plant designs that allowed to reach higher values of ef-
ciency. The cell stacks were split in two blocks. Various designs were simu-
lated to obtain a correct operation of the plant for both, anode pre-heater and
methanator, congurations. In both cases the solution with two blocks allows
to reach better eciency without signicant change in plant operating param-
eters. The use of two blocks of stacks increases the electric power produced
from SOFCs, because of this the eciency of the plants results higher (plant
eciency equal to 52.64% for the anode pre-heater conguration and 52.61%
for the methanator solution).
The new disposal also shows proper values of
energy available for district heating and cooling as well as good district heating
==PAGE:160==
136
Conclusions
eciency and COP.
Simulations were run with the attempt to nd optimized operating parameters
for all the designs under investigation. The most promising solutions were found
to be those with two blocks of stacks. The conguration with anode pre-heater
allows to improve the eciency by 5 percentage points, while the methanator
solution can reach an increase by 6 percentage points. Others plant designs
studied do not go beyond a growth by 4 percentage points.
The size of the plant is of paramount importance, in this study the range is
between 20 and 33 MW. The optimized solutions allow a higher power produc-
tion, by increasing the size of the plant better results in terms of eciency can
be obtained.
The economic evaluation of the investigated plants shows that the net present
value of the plants with two blocks of stacks is lower than other designs.
The simultaneous increase of energy produced and eciency, combined with an
evaluated reduction of payback time, makes the solutions with the split amount
of stacks really promising for the future of the trigeneration plant.
Future investigations could be carried out and these could be future improve-
ments:
 Dierent conguration with the split amount of stacks could be investi-
gated. More than only two blocks could be taken into account and dierent
designs should be studied and analysed in detail.
 Simulations could be run only for SOFC plant by testing the split amount
of stacks. In this way the consequences of this solution could be understood
better.
 Theoretical analysis on small scale SOFC could be carried out. Further
experimental studies could be done, on a small scale, to validate the results
obtained by the software.
 It could be useful to analyse the inuence of other parameters on the plant
eciency. Among the others, dierent values of the live steam pressure
(60 bar in this study) can be investigated.
 In order to reach higher eciency values, the possibility of integration
with dual pressure steam cycle could be taken into account.
==PAGE:161==
137
 Introducing pressure losses in the absorption plant model in order to have
a more realistic situation.
 The feasibility of the project by considering a two stage absorption plant
can be studied with the aim of reaching better COP and increasing the
cooling power production.
 Incentives could be taken into account in the economic analysis to obtain
more accurate results.
